<div id="review_81959816" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/81959816" />
    <a title="Morgan F" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/2941288-morgan-f"><img alt="Morgan F" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1262298598p2/2941288.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/81959816?book_show_action=true">Dec 24, 2009</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Morgan F" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Morgan F" href="/user/show/2941288-morgan-f">Morgan F</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9780385736824" href="/book/show/6518042-the-forest-of-hands-and-teeth">review of another edition</a>

          <div><span class="uitext greyText">Recommends it for: </span>
           <span class="uitext reviewText">fans of The Giver and I Am Legend. </span></div>

        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2941288-morgan-f?shelf=young-adult">young-adult</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2941288-morgan-f?shelf=dystopian-apocalyptic">dystopian-apocalyptic</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2941288-morgan-f?shelf=series">series</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2941288-morgan-f?shelf=favorite-covers">favorite-covers</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2941288-morgan-f?shelf=awesome-titles">awesome-titles</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2941288-morgan-f?shelf=read-2010">read-2010</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2941288-morgan-f?shelf=2000s">2000s</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2941288-morgan-f?shelf=goodreads-author">goodreads-author</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2941288-morgan-f?shelf=re-read">re-read</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2941288-morgan-f?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer81959816" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer15730475274613432404">I was really excited to read this book when it first came out. But being short on money (like always), I had to wait an entire year for it to come out in paperback. You should have seen my face when I spotted it's cover at Borders. It immediately went to the enormous pile I was lugging around (sadly, I had to put half the books back, because it would be called stealing otherwise). <br/><br/>This book is told from the perspective of Mary, a young woman growing up in a small, isolated village surrounded by </span>
  <span id="freeText15730475274613432404" style="display:none">I was really excited to read this book when it first came out. But being short on money (like always), I had to wait an entire year for it to come out in paperback. You should have seen my face when I spotted it's cover at Borders. It immediately went to the enormous pile I was lugging around (sadly, I had to put half the books back, because it would be called stealing otherwise). <br /><br />This book is told from the perspective of Mary, a young woman growing up in a small, isolated village surrounded by a fence that keeps the unrelenting zombies out. But they are not called zombies in this book (in fact the word zombie never mentioned), but rather the Unconsecrated. Trust me, they are true zombies. They eat flesh and babies and everything. Anyway, Mary grows up believing that her village, run by the dubious Sisterhood that claims that their little pocket of humanity amidst the formidible forest is the last of mankind. Mary, of course, questions this and is not content with her future as a member of the Sisterhood or married to man she doesn't love. Instead, she dreams of the ocean and the other stories her mother used to tell her of generations long gone. <br /><br />From the first chapter, Mary's life is turned upside down. Her father walks among the dead, and her mother goes to join him. She is turned away by her brother and is sent to live in the Cathedral with the Sisterhood, which has well-kept secrets in every room. <br /><br />This book is very well-written. Fluid and suspenseful, I had a hard time putting it down. While it did have some zombie-slaying action, it wasn't the focus of the book. Instead what kept me going was the sense of mystery and doom. Nothing good ever happens to Mary and the questions just kept coming with little-to-none answers. Mary was an unreliable narrator and a little crazy. All what the reader sees is first filtered through her eyes. She selfishly clung on to her dream of the ocean and refused to settle for anything less, even when it cost her the people she cared about. But hey, she is still one of the few chracters alive at the end, and the only one with a chance at a life, so she must have been doing something right. The rest of the characters wouldv'e gotten eaten long ago if Mary wasn't there to drive them.<br /><br />This book is severely creepy, what with zombies relentlessly moaning in the background. I got skeeved out in a couple scenes (zombie baby). Like I said earlier, nothing good really happens at all. This book isn't for the faint at heart as it can be somewhat depressing. But I still found it intelligent and refreshing. It's so nice to read a young adult novel without a saintly narrator and a perfectly happy ending.<br /><br />My least favorite part of it though was the love triangle? rectangle? I don't know what to call it. But the gist of it is Mary is in love with Travis. Travis is in love with Mary, but is engaged to Mary's best friend, Cass. Cass is in love with Harry, but Harry is engaged to Mary. Harry likes Mary, but I wouldn't call it love. I think he just wants a wife. Oh, and Travis and Harry are brothers. It's just a mess of duty and love. No one wants to marry who they are supposed to, but feel like they have a duty to do so. So, its complicated without ever being really interesting. I never really saw what was so great about Travis. Mary nursed him and her previous crush on him turned into full out love (or so she says). This might sound weird, but I could never tell when they were kissing or not. The scenes between them were written oddly, and I kept thinking they were kissing, but later on in the page I was proved wrong. Their lips were just really close together and they were <i>almost</i> kissing. My bad.<br /><br />Anyway, despite some personal preferences and little annoyances, this book was really good. Not for everyone, but I recommend everyone try it. I'm sooo looking forward to <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/6555517.The_Dead_Tossed_Waves__The_Forest_of_Hands_and_Teeth___2_" title="The Dead-Tossed Waves (The Forest of Hands and Teeth, #2) by Carrie Ryan" rel="nofollow noopener">The Dead-Tossed Waves</a>, where some questions might finally be answered. </span>
  <a data-text-id="15730475274613432404" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  <span id="freeText10433680337903751350" style="display:none">This book is the embodiment of so many things I hate. Here are some examples:<br /><br />1. The movie, <u>The Village</u>, by M. Night Shyamalan. I could rant about that piece of trash for hours. If you hated that movie, you will hate this book<br />2. Creepy religious groups<br />3. Nuns that remind me of the Nurse Ratched character from <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/332613.One_Flew_Over_the_Cuckoo_s_Nest" title="One Flew Over the Cuckoo's Nest by Ken Kesey" rel="nofollow noopener">One Flew Over the Cuckoo's Nest</a><br />4. (brothers!)<br />6. It seems to me that if you could kill those *&amp;^$ers, YOU WOULD BRING A LOT OF AMMO/ARROWS/WHATEVER to kill them! Where are the guns? This is in the future! Why do they only have axes and arrows? This technology is not lost.<br />7. Do the Unconsecrated have to be decapitated to die? We don't know because it is never really explained. And, if yes, why the frak are they shooting them with arrows?<br />8. This book has no ending. I will read the Wikipedia entry for the following book/s because I don't think I can bring myself to keep reading.</span>

              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1124284-misty?shelf=read-in-2009">read-in-2009</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1124284-misty?shelf=cover-appeal">cover-appeal</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1124284-misty?shelf=own">own</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1124284-misty?shelf=recommended">recommended</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer54838810" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer3688207980426940619">This seems to be one of those books that gets really mixed reactions. I've read more than a few rants that complain of the writing style (present tense), the love aspect, the originality aspect, and Mary herself, saying she's selfish and unlikeable. And most of the things that seem to bother people about this book help me to love it.<br/><br/>I found Ryan's writing beautifully and painfully evocative, and the present tense lent an immediacy to the narration that really worked. There are times when the thi</span>
  <span id="freeText3688207980426940619" style="display:none">This seems to be one of those books that gets really mixed reactions. I've read more than a few rants that complain of the writing style (present tense), the love aspect, the originality aspect, and Mary herself, saying she's selfish and unlikeable. And most of the things that seem to bother people about this book help me to love it.<br /><br />I found Ryan's writing beautifully and painfully evocative, and the present tense lent an immediacy to the narration that really worked. There are times when the things that Mary says in the novel are so perfectly phrased as to make me actually stop reading and just dwell on them. I could see everything so clearly, and sometimes just ached with it. It was lovely in a heartbreaking way.<br /><br /><br />Much like the romance between Mary and Travis. I loved every moment of that, and bought it all. This bit is a teensy bit spoilery, so if you haven't read it, look away.<br /><br />I know there are people who find the relationship unbelievable, and think that Mary was selfish for a) choosing Travis over Harry for no reason (? did they read the same book I did?), and for feeling like there was something more even than Travis. I understand why people were frustrated by this and thought Mary selfish -- so many people read YA for the easy romance and the lies. I hate to say it, but it's true. I respect Ryan so much more for not making things easy like that. I absolutely loved that, although Mary loved Travis, she realized there was more to the world, and since she lives in a pretty effed up world, there most certainly is. Mary is a woman on a mission, and she doesn't let anything sway her from that. It's a bit maniacal, maybe, but understandably so, and it makes for a much more complex, nuanced, adult novel than people typically get from YA. I appreciated that. <br /><br />Same goes for the ending. Some people were really upset about the lack of resolution in the end, and I personally loved it. (And even though I know there is a sequel (and 3rd!), and fully intend to read them, I would have been content with 1 open-ended but powerful book.) It would have been a cop-out to have everything wrapped up neatly. I like a book that makes you wonder and makes you think, and even that makes you uncomfortable. It means the writer was working and doing their job, not just churning out some schlocky mess for $$.<br /><br /><br />This isn't to say I thought it was a perfect book. There were times when the prose was a bit purply, and I was worried on occasion that it was about to go over the top. I originally rated it a 4 on Goodreads, but as time passed, I found myself craving it, and thinking about Mary and the things she went through, the choices she had to make, and respecting it more and more. It's one of those books that I know I will reread and appreciate in different ways, but that I would reread even if that wasn't the case, just to get back to the beauty of Ryan's writing.<br /><br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="3688207980426940619" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

              <span id="reviewTextContainer1287934318" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer8248920670470242701"><b>It's Zombiefest July!</b> I've been reading zombie books with my MacHalo sisters and felt I needed something a little more, so decided to read this one on my own, in-between other reads.<br/><br/>It's the end of the world as we know it. Civilization has long been decimated and no one knows about things like skyscrapers or oceans anymore. All that is known is the forest. The forest is where the "Unconsecrated" are. They have pretty much taken over the world and people have been forced to build huge fences and </span>
  <span id="freeText8248920670470242701" style="display:none"><b>It's Zombiefest July!</b> I've been reading zombie books with my MacHalo sisters and felt I needed something a little more, so decided to read this one on my own, in-between other reads.<br><br>It's the end of the world as we know it. Civilization has long been decimated and no one knows about things like skyscrapers or oceans anymore. All that is known is the forest. The forest is where the "Unconsecrated" are. They have pretty much taken over the world and people have been forced to build huge fences and whatever other types of fortresses they can come up with to keep the "Unconsecrated" out. Mary's village reminded me of the M. Night Shyamalan movie The Village.<br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1437664414i/15611391._SX540_.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>The Sisterhood is sort of like the law and also provide spiritual comfort and guidance. But they're secretive and a little, well, some of them are just plain old bitches. Mary is one young girl who lives in one of these villages, surrounded by a fence the Guardians must patrol and maintain. Her best friend, Cass and two boys they grew up with, Harry and Travis are about to get married. Only the boy Mary wants is pledged to someone else. And their lives are about to get ALL fracked up.<br><br>I won't go into the story anymore, but WOW! I loved this. My feels got all crazy and I even CRIED!<br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1437664414ra/15611392.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>What a GREAT zombie book. At first, I felt like Mary was really meh and then she turns out to have some smarts and spunk in her. At times, it was a bit annoying to be in her head because she obsesses about one particular boy and her dreams of finding the ocean. I'm deducting one star because I did have to skim a few paragraphs were she kept going on and on about her romantic life. She gets all like this about the guy she wants:<br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1437664414ra/15611393.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>But thankfully, those sections didn't go on endlessly. This is more of a plot driven story than character driven, so the characters weren't fleshed out all that great, but it works for a book like this. <br><br>I thought it was an excellent, creepy, dystopian zombie book. I tore through this and it was a page-turner. I am so going to read the rest of the series! </span>

<div id="review_63540960" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/63540960" />
    <a title="Shannon" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/2016128-shannon"><img alt="Shannon" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1572638169p2/2016128.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/63540960?book_show_action=true">Jul 14, 2009</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Shannon" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Shannon" href="/user/show/2016128-shannon">Shannon</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Hardcover 9780385736817" href="/book/show/6468718-the-forest-of-hands-and-teeth">review of another edition</a>

          <div><span class="uitext greyText">Recommends it for: </span>
           <span class="uitext reviewText">zombie, suspense, horror, and mystery fans</span></div>

        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2016128-shannon?shelf=horror">horror</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2016128-shannon?shelf=suspense">suspense</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2016128-shannon?shelf=young-adult">young-adult</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2016128-shannon?shelf=novels">novels</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2016128-shannon?shelf=zombies">zombies</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2016128-shannon?shelf=borrowed">borrowed</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer63540960" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer2274415988953164427">The Forest of Hands and Teeth instantly reminded me of the movie The Village and it also made me think of the movie Dawn of the Dead as well. But even if you didn't like those movies or never saw them, don't let it detract from wanting to check out this book.<br/><br/>Mary, the main character, lives in a village some time in the not-so-distant future where civilization has been set back by hundreds of years, because of something called "The Return." The village is surrounded by a fence which holds back th</span>
  <span id="freeText2274415988953164427" style="display:none">The Forest of Hands and Teeth instantly reminded me of the movie The Village and it also made me think of the movie Dawn of the Dead as well. But even if you didn't like those movies or never saw them, don't let it detract from wanting to check out this book.<br /><br />Mary, the main character, lives in a village some time in the not-so-distant future where civilization has been set back by hundreds of years, because of something called "The Return." The village is surrounded by a fence which holds back the Forest of Hands and Teeth. Within the forest are Unconsecrated, or really, zombies. The inhabitants of the village live their lives while the Unconsecrated moan, push their fingers through and shake the fence. <br /><br />But Mary has dreams of the ocean. She remembers a photograph that her mother showed her of her great-great-great grandmother standing in the ocean. She can't shake the image and she longs to see it for herself. But leaving the village means death or becoming another of the unconsecrated so Mary has to be content with dreaming.<br /><br />Until the fence is breached and she's forced to leave the village and survive.<br /><br />This novel was at times frustrating, heartbreaking, and horrifying, but it's one of those books that you just have to read that next chapter to find out what happens. <br /><br />That part that was frustrating for me was the first part of the book when Mary is still in the village. Women have two choices; either be spoken for by a man or join the Sisterhood. If a man doesn't speak for you, you default to the Sisterhood. The Sisters and the Guardians are a bunch of Puritanical crazies, but I can see how they'd want to create order in a small village that could be the last of humanity.<br /><br />There's a heartbreaking love story told throughout this book as well. I can't really say anything without giving something away, but this aspect of the novel really adds something to the story and it makes you care that much more for the characters.<br /><br />There's a lot of gruesome parts to this book and if you're squeamish about decapitation and things of the sort, you might want to look for another book. It's not too graphic, but there are some disturbing scenes.<br /><br />At the end, there's still a lot of unanswered questions. This chapter of Mary's life has ended, but her story is not over. <br /><br />Now I can't wait for <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/6555517.The_Dead_Tossed_Waves" title="The Dead-Tossed Waves by Carrie Ryan" rel="nofollow noopener">The Dead-Tossed Waves</a>. I read the description, <b>don't read it unless you don't mind spoiling yourself</b>, and it sounds just as good as The Forest of Hands and Teeth. There aren't that many zombie books around, but this is definitely one of the best.</span>
  <a data-text-id="2274415988953164427" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_2230166009" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2230166009" />
    <a title="Faith M ✨" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/29390149-faith-m"><img alt="Faith M ✨" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1587515873p2/29390149.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2230166009?book_show_action=true">Jan 19, 2019</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Faith M ✨" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Faith M ✨" href="/user/show/29390149-faith-m">Faith M ✨</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9780385736824" href="/book/show/6518042-the-forest-of-hands-and-teeth">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/29390149-faith-m?shelf=butt-ugly-covers">butt-ugly-covers</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/29390149-faith-m?shelf=mc-gurl">mc-gurl</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/29390149-faith-m?shelf=dystopia">dystopia</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/29390149-faith-m?shelf=young-adult">young-adult</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/29390149-faith-m?shelf=read-2019">read-2019</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/29390149-faith-m?shelf=1st-person">1st-person</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/29390149-faith-m?shelf=postapocalyptic">postapocalyptic</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/29390149-faith-m?shelf=3-stars">3-stars</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/29390149-faith-m?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/29390149-faith-m?shelf=zambams">zambams</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2230166009" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer10511597336660625855"><blockquote>We are our own memory-keepers, and we have failed ourselves.</blockquote><br/>Honestly, I lowkey hated the first two thirds of this. It was dreadful. Dreadful isn't even the right word for it. It was like a soap opera set in a middle school being relayed to you on the cringest tumblr account imaginable. It was a time capsule from 2009. #10yearchallenge to the extreme. There was no personality. The atmosphere was minimal. Not a single character had a personality. The passing of time as imperceptible -- months pass</span>
  <span id="freeText10511597336660625855" style="display:none"><blockquote>We are our own memory-keepers, and we have failed ourselves.</blockquote><br />Honestly, I lowkey hated the first two thirds of this. It was dreadful. Dreadful isn't even the right word for it. It was like a soap opera set in a middle school being relayed to you on the cringest tumblr account imaginable. It was a time capsule from 2009. #10yearchallenge to the extreme. There was no personality. The atmosphere was minimal. Not a single character had a personality. The passing of time as imperceptible -- months passed and I hadn't even known it was a new day. The "love story" is almost nonsensical. Their attraction is explained through exposition and the tension consists of the two of them sitting next to each other. How riveting. Just like the 6th grade. It was just a little bit mind-numbing.<br /><br />This was written similarly to Lois Lowry's <i>The Giver</i>, and while I love most of her work, I admit that she's has a pretty boring style. It works for middle grade but not really for YA.<br /><br />However! The last third was actually pretty darn good. It actually got just a little bit meta and started criticizing its own faults, analyzing its own characters and asking them, "what even are your motivations?" It's a little bad that it even had to do that, but at least I got some substance out of this.<br /><br />The last part had a lot of tension, a lot of atmosphere, and even made me cry a little. Some of the characters did things that made no sense given their crappy characterization, but it was still pretty okay. I was surprised how it ended, and actually really appreciated how it subverted some tropes.<br /><br /><blockquote>That's just the way life is. Some days you wake up and the beach is clear and you forget about everything that surrounds us. And some days you wake up and it looks like this. That's the nature of the tides.</blockquote><br />Read this review and more on my blog <a href="https://youarewhat-youread.blogspot.com/" rel="nofollow noopener">here</a>!</span>
  <a data-text-id="10511597336660625855" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_506854759" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/506854759" />
    <a title="Merna " class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/16392157-merna"><img alt="Merna " src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1358143553p2/16392157.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/506854759?book_show_action=true">Jan 14, 2013</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Merna " class="user" itemprop="url" name="Merna " href="/user/show/16392157-merna">Merna </a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was ok"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was ok</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/16392157-merna?shelf=dnf">dnf</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/16392157-merna?shelf=hate-with-all-my-guts">hate-with-all-my-guts</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer506854759" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer13177703218247981866">I still haven't finished reading this book. But I felt it would be necessary to write as I go along reading the ‘Forest Of Hands And Teeth’. Just to make the book to some extent more bearable. <br/><br/>Props to the writer who faintly has beautiful way with words, but also has a way with boring me to tears. Yet, I can't tell if I'm bored stiff because of the way it’s written that causes my eyes to go heavy with sleep, or if perhaps it’s the plot. It could be the characters in addition. Or, possibly it’s a</span>
  <span id="freeText13177703218247981866" style="display:none">I still haven't finished reading this book. But I felt it would be necessary to write as I go along reading the ‘Forest Of Hands And Teeth’. Just to make the book to some extent more bearable. <br /><br />Props to the writer who faintly has beautiful way with words, but also has a way with boring me to tears. Yet, I can't tell if I'm bored stiff because of the way it’s written that causes my eyes to go heavy with sleep, or if perhaps it’s the plot. It could be the characters in addition. Or, possibly it’s all three combined together to make tremendously dreary story. <br /><br /><b>Here’s a little blurb about what the book is about.</b><br /><br />The forest of hands and teeth is about a village under the leadership of the strict and enigmatic sisters. This village happens to be surrounded by zombies who continually attempt to break through the fences in order to devour the people. Mary’s great-great-great-great-great grandmother saw the ocean and her story has been passed down five generations. This becomes Mary’s bothersome and egoistic dream to see the ocean. <br /><br />Wait, sorry did I say that was a blurb or the WHOLE plot? It’s puzzling because I truly can’t tell the difference between the plot and the blurb. <br /><br />You can almost just predict what's going to occur in the story from merely the blurb. <br /><br />Fence + Zombies = that adds up to them finally managing to break through the fence, suddenly... doesn't it?<br /><br />Mary + her ocean dream = her going through a boring journey to see the ocean.<br /><br /><b>I want to introduce to you the most selfish character in the book.</b><br /><br />Of course it is none other than the main character Mary.<br /><br /><b>Here are some quotes to support my point.</b> <br /><br /><i>“Going down that path would kill us all, Mary,” Cass says. “You're selfish to want to sacrifice all of us for your own whims.”</i> (Thanks Cass for pointing how much a selfish bitch Mary is). <br /><br /><i>“You are a Guardian. Killing the Unconsecrated is what you are trained to do. You've put us all in danger by keeping her alive. You know the rules.”</i> (This is what Mary says to her own brother to convince him to kill his wife. She says as if it was so simple). <br /><br /><i>“I have known love,” I whisper, as much to myself as to my brother.<br /><br />He lifts a corner of his lips, almost smiling. “You can't ever have known love.” I am about to protest when he holds up a hand to stop me and continues, “Because if you had you wouldn't be telling me to kill my wife as if it were an easy choice.”</i> (You just got slammed Mary). <br /><br />Cass (her best friend) is sobbing because virtually she has lost everything in her life. Travis attempts to comfort her, while Mary stands there getting jealous because he is. <br /><br />I have nothing against selfish characters. It makes them human. But Mary is just abusing how selfish you can be. <br /><br />I’ll finish the review after I complete the book. If I can. <br /><br /><b>*EDIT*</b><br /><br />Okay, I'm officially through with this book. I've lost all hope for finishing it. <br /><br />Mary was growing out to be a little bit more selfless, but it wasn't sufficient to make me continue reading the book. <br /><br /><b>Here’s a random quote:</b><br /><br /><i>"Travis, whose breath I measure as we sleep, whose heart<br />is the cadence to my life."</i> *gag* I don't know about you Mary, but if I was being haunted or tracked by zombies, I would try to save my energy to fight them off the next day if they ever attack. I wouldn't be wasting my sleeping time measuring someone's breath. Edward much? <br /><br />I also realized the two characters can’t take responsibility for their own faults and blame God constantly for their obligation. One of the characters slipped and fell. He thought it was god’s punishment for being unhappy with the choices he had made (What choices? Oh you mean the ones you never really made). Mary is too selfish to comprehend it was her mistake and not god. It’s ironic because she doesn't believe in god any longer, but she blames him still. I dislike characters who can’t take the fact it was their responsibility and no one else. <br /><br />I found out what happened at the end. WORST ENDING EVER. <br /><br />Completely done with this book. <br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="13177703218247981866" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_48960922" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/48960922" />
    <a title="Angela" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/1027031-angela"><img alt="Angela" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1442501610p2/1027031.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/48960922?book_show_action=true">Mar 11, 2009</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Angela" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Angela" href="/user/show/1027031-angela">Angela</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="ebook 9780375891977" href="/book/show/7001361-the-forest-of-hands-and-teeth">review of another edition</a>

          <div><span class="uitext greyText">Recommends it for: </span>
           <span class="uitext reviewText">Zombie fans</span></div>

        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1027031-angela?shelf=horror">horror</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1027031-angela?shelf=ya">ya</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1027031-angela?shelf=zombies">zombies</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer48960922" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer12086599952707769172">I can solidly say that my acquisition of <i>The Forest of Hands and Teeth</i> is entirely the work of John Scalzi's <i>Big Idea</i> posts that have been prominently featured on his blog. This book was just recently featured, and as soon as I saw the post go up I knew I had to check this one out. I don't read a lot of YA, but this one had all the right elements for me: a young heroine anxious to explore beyond the confines of her restrictive world. A post-apocalyptic setting, where what's left of humanity has </span>
  <span id="freeText12086599952707769172" style="display:none">I can solidly say that my acquisition of <i>The Forest of Hands and Teeth</i> is entirely the work of John Scalzi's <i>Big Idea</i> posts that have been prominently featured on his blog. This book was just recently featured, and as soon as I saw the post go up I knew I had to check this one out. I don't read a lot of YA, but this one had all the right elements for me: a young heroine anxious to explore beyond the confines of her restrictive world. A post-apocalyptic setting, where what's left of humanity has had to cobble together a civilization out of the ashes of the old. And, most importantly, zombies!<br /><br />Because, as I have expressed before, I do love me some zombies.<br /><br />But here's the thing. This is a zombie novel, yes, but it's an oddly haunting and lyrical one. The title alone captures this and is in no small part what drew me to the book; then, too, you've got the cover art. Mary, the girl on the cover, stands looking pensive in front of a bleak woodland. This captures the mood of the book <i>perfectly</i>, because this story isn't about the zombie outbreak; it's about the tiny society that's arisen seven generations after, and the few remnants of the pre-outbreak life they've managed to cobble together into a village. What happened to create the Unconsecrated, as Mary's people call the zombies, is never called out. Instead, the zombies are a constant background detail, a shuffling, shambling mass of unlife beyond the fences that surround the village.<br /><br />Mary is the heart of the story, a young woman who's grown up on her mother's tales of the ocean, which no one in their village has ever seen. When Mary loses her mother to the Unconsecrated, it puts her on a path between having to decide between two young men, challenging the long-held secrets of the Sisterhood that rules her village, and ultimately, to finding that mythical ocean. It's an excellent story overall and well worth checking out for YA and adult readers alike. Five stars.<br /><br />ETA 11/3/2014: On a reread I find that yep, I still like this story a lot. I have a couple more quibbles with it than I did on the first read through, but I was very happy to revisit it by way of preparing to read the rest in the series.</span>
  <a data-text-id="12086599952707769172" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

    <div class="section">
      

<div id="review_254354743" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/254354743" />
    <a title="Michael" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/1036930-michael"><img alt="Michael" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1583425448p2/1036930.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/254354743?book_show_action=true">Jan 01, 2012</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Michael" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Michael" href="/user/show/1036930-michael">Michael</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1036930-michael?shelf=fiction-that-speculates">fiction-that-speculates</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1036930-michael?shelf=2000s">2000s</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer254354743" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer8047472286827018652">Can we talk about zombies? <br/><br/>I mean, let's really think about these guys for a minute, because the whole idea of zombies is where my problems with this book begins. I for one am not concerned about the zombie apocalypse. And, if it happens, I have complete faith we can kick the asses out of some stupid, slow versions of ourselves. <br/><br/>We'll start with the basic idea of a zombie. Theoretically, these are corpses that get up, walk around, bite people and infect them. Great! Those will be really scary fo</span>
  <span id="freeText8047472286827018652" style="display:none">Can we talk about zombies? <br /><br />I mean, let's really think about these guys for a minute, because the whole idea of zombies is where my problems with this book begins. I for one am not concerned about the zombie apocalypse. And, if it happens, I have complete faith we can kick the asses out of some stupid, slow versions of ourselves. <br /><br />We'll start with the basic idea of a zombie. Theoretically, these are corpses that get up, walk around, bite people and infect them. Great! Those will be really scary for a little bit. But what is causing them to rise? Is it a disease that only affects humans? Okay, lets assume it is. IF THIS IS THE CASE, all of the dead bodies that are ALREADY dead will NOT be attacking anyone. Thus, we have to contend with people who are infected and dying in the present, and who will decompose. After all, there's no logic to the assumption that zombies just don't decompose. Do maggots not want to eat them? Are they impervious to the elements of rain, wind, dust storms, cold, heat, and everything else that makes living people uncomfortable? NOBODY who is arguing FOR zombies can use logic and argue that any of these things could be the case. It makes no sense at all. These motherfuckers would be falling apart left and right, and after about two weeks, the original batch would be non-existent.<br /><br />Okay, maybe a month.<br /><br />On the other hand, perhaps the already-dead humans will raise up. As I've ranted about before, this makes no sense, because dead humans are simply decomposing matter, just like dead dogs and dead trees and the non-silicone parts of Michael Jackson. If dead humans start walking around because dead matter is getting reborn, we're also going to have dirt golems and sentient dead trees, and shit is gonna get really ugly. We'll be fighting against our own dead cells that are trying to eat our living cells, and we will simply be screwed. Thus, zombies won't even matter in this scenario. Thus, as my very scientifically grounded argument illustrates, dead bodies will not all start digging their ways out of the ground as zombies. <br /><br />So we'll stick to the disease hypothesis. The idea of zombies getting up and walking around and actually being a long-term threat doesn't make sense. In fact, I think it's a stretch to say zombies are a global threat on even a short-term basis. . . zombies taking over the world requires faith in what is basically a pyramid scheme: one zombie bites three people, each of those people bites three people before they get decapitated, and eventually the hordes of zombies overwhelm the normal people. We all know pyramid schemes are bullshit because eventually some people just don't follow through with it. One group of marines or ultimate fighters kills off 90 of them. A bomb blows up hundreds. We can't say exactly what factor will keep the scheme from working, but we know from experience dealing with people--ALIVE ONES with functioning brains--that pyramid schemes don't work.<br /><br />So, I have a lot of trouble buying this idea that zombies will become some huge threat if they are (a) only raised after an infected person comes back from the dead; (b) relying on a pyramid scheme to take over the world; and (c) slower, stupider versions of humans. As we have seen in many wars in the past, numbers matter less than strategery. And if there's one thing we humans have figured out how to do in our many years of living on this planet, it's kill other humans. I mean, c'mon! With weaponry from five hundred years ago we could handle any zombie uprising we come across, unless we ignore the zombies until they have swept through more than half of the human population. Since this is highly unlikely in the age of blogging and ratings-governed news coverage, I again would like to point out zombies will NOT be a problem.<br /><br />When it comes to this book, though, these problems get even more accentuated. We're starting the story many, many years after the zombies first started attacking people. They're on the other side of a frickin' chain link fence, moaning and lumbering, as zombies are wont to do. Why have we not simply started stabbing them all through the head with sharp sticks through the holes in the fence? Why don't we fight their pyramid scheme with one of our own? If everyone goes out to the fence every day and stabs two zombies in the head, eventually none of them will be moaning and groaning around our village. It doesn't totally end the problem, but that's where protective body armor, helmets, and artillery comes into play. Zombies don't know how to engage in guerilla warfare, but we do. These zombies--in case you've forgotten--are trying to kill people with their teeth. Their fucking TEETH. If some random-ass dude comes at me with his teeth, I'm gonna come at him with something OTHER THAN MY TEETH. . . basically any weapon wins against teeth. . . and I'm going to win. If this person also doesn't have a functioning brain, I'm guessing that will bump my chances up even further. <br /><br />So, there's THAT logical hole. Even if zombies have a heyday because of a ridiculously successful beginning--for instance, the disease starts simultaneously in several places that don't have oil, and every zombie is very diligent about biting three people before getting decapitated--they're gonna be less of a long-term threat than the Spice Girls. We're going to suddenly recognize that we ought to be killing these slow, stupid humans, and we will develop strategies for doing so. <br /><br />My vote in the contest between smart, fast humans and slow, stupid ones has always been on the former. This is why I'm not a Cardinals fan. Zombies are a fun kind of mob for characters in horror movies to fight, and it's fun to watch these people get torn apart in hilarious ways. But when the idea of zombies is converted into a book that tries for more than just slasher goofiness, the holes in the whole theory start to pop open like holes in a maggot-ridden corpse. <br /><br />Thus, I must admit I was much more critical while reading TFHT than I have been when watching Dawn of the Dead, Day of the Dead, Night of the Living Dead, High Noon of the Dead, Tea Time of the Dead, and a variety of other influential zombie flicks. However, I feel Ryan's attempt to place the events in this series quite a bit after the actual zombie apocalypse begs her audience to ask these questions about how possible this whole scenario really is. <br /><br />And, following my usual pattern of ranting for a long time and then briefly mentioning the book in question, here are a couple other thoughts on <i>The Forest of Hands and Teeth</i>: it's appropriately eerie, and an entertaining read. However, the secondary characters are only occasionally likeable, and this is a problem that carries over into the second book of the trilogy. Although you don't necessarily want these people to get eaten by zombies, you do kind of wish many of them would abruptly depart from the storyline so you didn't have to read about the annoying things they're saying/doing any longer. And the series suffers from a thematic issue that most zombie literature is likely to struggle with: in a world where humanity has been bested by stupid, dead versions of ourselves, how can you give your reader a genuine sense of hope?<br /><br /><br /><br /><br /><br /><br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="8047472286827018652" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer220222279" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer3322185630859042738">What did I think of <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/3432478.The_Forest_of_Hands_and_Teeth__The_Forest_of_Hands_and_Teeth___1_' title='The Forest of Hands and Teeth (The Forest of Hands and Teeth, #1) by Carrie Ryan' rel='nofollow noopener'>The Forest of Hands and Teeth</a>?<br/><br/><img src='https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1380360780ra/711683.gif' alt='Image and video hosting by TinyPic' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/><br/><img src='https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1380360780ra/711684.gif' alt='Image and video hosting by TinyPic' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/><br/><img src='https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1380360780ra/711685.gif' alt='Image and video hosting by TinyPic' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/><br/><img src='https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1380360780i/711686._SX540_.png' alt='Image and video hosting by TinyPic' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/><br/><br/><br/>I'm sorry to those who enjoyed this book, but I was not amused.<br/>In fact, I was severely disappointed.<br/>And it HURTS me to be disappointed because zombies. <b>Freaking. Zombies.</b><br/><br/>But no, guys. No. <br/><b>Love comes first.</b> In every story, you will ever read again, the main character's love life is the top priority.<br/>And not just their love life! NO IT HAS TO BE A TRIANGLE TOO. Everything has to be goddamn love triangles every waking moment. Please think of my brain</span>
  <span id="freeText3322185630859042738" style="display:none">What did I think of <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/3432478.The_Forest_of_Hands_and_Teeth__The_Forest_of_Hands_and_Teeth___1_" title="The Forest of Hands and Teeth (The Forest of Hands and Teeth, #1) by Carrie Ryan" rel="nofollow noopener">The Forest of Hands and Teeth</a>?<br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1380360780ra/711683.gif" alt="Image and video hosting by TinyPic" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1380360780ra/711684.gif" alt="Image and video hosting by TinyPic" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1380360780ra/711685.gif" alt="Image and video hosting by TinyPic" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1380360780i/711686._SX540_.png" alt="Image and video hosting by TinyPic" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br><br>I'm sorry to those who enjoyed this book, but I was not amused.<br>In fact, I was severely disappointed.<br>And it HURTS me to be disappointed because zombies. <b>Freaking. Zombies.</b><br><br>But no, guys. No. <br><b>Love comes first.</b> In every story, you will ever read again, the main character's love life is the top priority.<br>And not just their love life! NO IT HAS TO BE A TRIANGLE TOO. Everything has to be goddamn love triangles every waking moment. Please think of my braincells. Please think of them and all they've suffered through. My god.<br><br>But let's get into this book. It was a good attempt, and I'm being nice in saying that. And honestly, I really don't have to much to say before the breakdown so let's just get it over with.<br><br><b>Boop</b>...<br><br>The writing irked me muchly. First person present is a pain to me, especially when it's done incorrectly. In my short experience with it, you have to go the extra mile to really get your readers into the story if you are going with present tense. More effort is needed to get your reader to ignore the tense. <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/4487674.Moira_Young" title="Moira Young" rel="nofollow noopener">Moira Young</a> did it right, while Carrie Ryan did it wrong.<br><br>The prose didn't give me any sense of dread or horror that it should have brought full force. It focused too much on things that tried to be important but just weren't. Honestly, I don't even think Mary's mother's death was even important. There were a few things that were unnecessary in this story.<br><br>I felt no attachment whatsoever to any of the characters portrayed in this story except for Cass, because she seemed to be the only character who acted like anyone was supposed to during a zombie nightmare. Whenever Cass wasn't involved, I was skipping pages. Living Mary's life was boring. <b>BORING! <i>IN A ZOMBIE NOVEL.</i></b><br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1380360780ra/711687.gif" alt="Image and video hosting by TinyPic" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>HOW CAN YOU MESS UP ZOMBIES?<br><br>A: By writing those GODFORSAKEN LOVE TRIANGLES THAT DON'T EVEN WORK RIGHT.<br><br>It's one thing if you need to have that human relation, but c'mon, it's not all that hard. It really isn't. Build them, Ryan. You have to build characters. That's how stories work.<br><br>I will now continue onto these said characters with official surnames provided by moi.<br><br><b>Mary "I M OCEAN" Mariana</b><br><br>Mary was boring, and obsessed about two things only: Travis Limpitruck and the ocean. That was it. And it wasn't even trips to the ocean or just loving it, but it was <i>believing</i> that the ocean existed. Alright, I understand that seeing the ocean for the first time would be huge. Like, "Golly gee look at this!" I understand her craving, but this ocean love comes off as obsessed, hopelessly obsessed. It scares me.<br><br>She complains and COMPLAINS, envies her best friend (I can see why. Cass' clearly the better character), and has a boy who'd commit seppuku for her. I honestly don't see why this girl isn't accepting Harry's appreciation and running towards Travis like he's the last boy in the village. WHY. We are never told why Mary loves the fuck out of Travis. She just does. And we're forced to cope.<br><br>Also I had to laugh at her obsession with Gabrielle, the Outsider she had a ten second conversation with. I understand that she is the drive to get out of the village and proof of the outside, but in all seriousness, I wouldn't be surprised if Mary had become infatuated with her. Hell I bet when Mary has a kid, she's gonna name her Gabrielle to honor her or some shit. (Also, how come Gabrielle was the Fast One? Cause she had a red vest like Marty McFly?) Oh wait, we're not diving into that, it's about love, it's about love. WHICH BRINGS ME TO...<br><br><b>Travis "Beecuz I Lub Hur" Limpitruck</b><br><br>Travis was the boy that Mary just loved and loved like crazy. So much love. SO MUCH OF IT. And why? Lol, who cares? We have zombies, right? Oh no, it is about love after all. Travis vs. Harry. THE SHOWDOWN OF THE BROTHERS. Except it's poorly done, incredibly stupid, and downright boring. Later on, thank god, I find out why Travis was gawking like crazy over Mary and that eased up this love for a little bit. Hell, it even gave him some character. FINALLY.<br><br><a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[His death was actually done quite nicely. I was a little bummed when he died, but Mary was just so selfish about her ocean and shit that I just shook my head and kept reading. "<i>Oh why didn't I realize that he was everything?!</i>" Mary, you're so STUPID. <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span><br><br>Frankly, I can't go into the other characters because they weren't developed enough for me. No one else tried to develop except maybe Jed and Cass "Come at Me" Blues. Jed had good emotional reactions to his hardships, as did Cass. Maybe that's why I didn't mind them so bad. Harry was no one, Jacob was no one, Argos was no one, you get my point.<br><br>I didn't care about this characters, which is an important thing to build if you want someone to enjoy your story if I remember correctly...NO WAIT. It's about love. It's all about love, I forget. It's not about survival or life or overpowering the zombies.<br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1380360780ra/711688.gif" alt="Image and video hosting by TinyPic" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>This book was just so INFURIATING TO ME. There are too many questions left that needed answering, the prose was weird, there were grammar mistakes, there was the shittiest ending since <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/7735333.Matched__Matched___1_" title="Matched (Matched, #1) by Ally Condie" rel="nofollow noopener">Matched</a>, UGHGHGHGHGHGKDFJBNVLKDSJBG.<br><br>I will say this though, as much as I seem to rage fest on this review, your opinion may be totally completely different. This book has very mixed reviews, so who knows? You might just have more love for it than I do. And I am A-okay with that.<br><br>I personally don't recommend it, but if you're curious, why the hell not? Might as well try your luck, right?<br><br>I'm done here.<br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1380360780ra/711689.gif" alt="Image and video hosting by TinyPic" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></span>
  <a data-text-id="3322185630859042738" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

  function submitShelfLink(unique_id, book_id, shelf_id, shelf_name, submit_form, exclusive) {
    var checkbox_id = 'shelf_name_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    var element = document.getElementById(checkbox_id)

    var checked = element.checked
    if (checked && exclusive) {
      // can't uncheck a radio by clicking it!
      return
    }
    if(document.getElementById("savingMessage")){
      Element.show('savingMessage')
    }
    var element_id = 'shelfInDropdownName_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    Element.update(element_id, "saving...");
    if (submit_form) {
      Element.hide('shelfDropdown_' + unique_id)
      var form = document.getElementById('addBookForm' + book_id)
      if (form) {
        form.shelf.value = shelf_name
        form.onsubmit()
      }
    }
    else {
      var action = checked ? 'remove' : ''
      element.checked = !element.checked
      new Ajax.Request('/shelf/add_to_shelf', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name)}, parameters:'book_id=' + book_id + '&name=' + shelf_name + '&a=' + action + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('QXTpT5nYe3vNj21YnOv8TEvdyk74tw0LG+Vcym+XN/5q1MRn3VDENSQWZUW+yS7ah77gPBBwsAC1SWmNwFDiIA==')})
    }
  }

  function shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name) {
    Element.update('shelfListfalse_' + book_id, request.responseText)
    afterShelfSave(checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name.escapeHTML())
  }

  function refreshGroupBox(group_id, book_id) {
    new Ajax.Updater('addGroupBooks' + book_id + '', '/group/add_book_box', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){refreshGroupBoxComplete(request, book_id);}, parameters:'id=' + group_id + '&book_id=' + book_id + '&refresh=true' + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('F/z7QfQLvKfNY3wn6UxHcFkFhU7Lb2518hXMvjci9bI8XNZpsIMD6ST6dDrLbpXmlWavPCOo035cufn5mOUgbA==')})
  }

<span id="freeTextContainer85358467869823303">Carrie Ryan is the <i>New York Times</i> bestselling author of a lot of books. She use to be a lawyer. Happily, she is not anymore.   <span id="freeText85358467869823303" style="display:none">Carrie Ryan is the <i>New York Times</i> bestselling author of a lot of books. She use to be a lawyer. Happily, she is not anymore. You can keep it that way by reading her books:<br /><br />If you like zombies, try the <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/3432478._Forest_of_Hands_and_Teeth" title=" Forest of Hands and Teeth" rel="nofollow noopener"> Forest of Hands and Teeth</a> series.<br /><br />If you like clever, fun adventure fantasy for 8-12 year olds, definitely read the <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/20980662._Map_To_Everywhere" title=" Map To Everywhere" rel="nofollow noopener"> Map To Everywhere</a> series (co-written with her husband, John Parke Davis).<br /><br />If you like cold calculated revenge involving hidden identities and lots of secrets: <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/23281652._Daughter_of_Deep_Silence" title=" Daughter of Deep Silence" rel="nofollow noopener"> Daughter of Deep Silence</a>.<br /><br />If you or your kids like multi-author, multi-platform series like 39 Clues and Spirit Animals, try <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/13356177._Infinity_Ring__Divide_and_Conquer" title=" Infinity Ring: Divide and Conquer" rel="nofollow noopener"> Infinity Ring: Divide and Conquer</a> -- it's produced by the same publisher (and has vikings and true history!)<br /><br />If you like true-crime stuff (both fiction and podcasts), <b>check out her upcoming release, <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/40490159._Dead_Air" title=" Dead Air" rel="nofollow noopener"> Dead Air</a>, a serialized thriller co-written with <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/1951011._Gwenda_Bond" title=" Gwenda Bond" rel="nofollow noopener"> Gwenda Bond</a> and <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/15292._Rachel_Caine" title=" Rachel Caine" rel="nofollow noopener"> Rachel Caine</a>.</b><br /><br />If you're pretty sure you won't survive the zombie apocalypse, you're in good company. She won't either.<br /><br /><b>instagram:</b> <a href="https://www.instagram.com/carrieryanwrites/" rel="nofollow noopener">@CarrieRyanWrites</a><br /><b>twitter:</b> <a href="http://www.twitter.com/carrieryan" rel="nofollow noopener">@CarrieRyan</a><br /><b>website:</b> <a href="http://www.carrieryan.com" rel="nofollow noopener">www.CarrieRyan.com</a></span>

I don't know if his feet are ticklish or how long his toes are. I don't know what nightmares he had as a child. I don't know which stars are his favorites, what shapes he sees in the clouds. I don't know what he is truly afraid of or what memories he holds closest. <br />And I don't have enough time now, never enough time. I want to be in the moment with him, feel his body against mine and think of nothing else, but my mind explodes with grief for all that I am missing. All that I will miss. All that I have wasted.&rdquo;</span>
